## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive relation: stress sigma as a function of strain epsilon with temperature T modulating stiffness, yield/flow stress, and thermal strain/softening. Common models combine an elastic (often linear) stress–strain law with temperature-dependent modulus and/or temperature-dependent plastic hardening/softening factors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (thermoelastic stiffness varying approximately linearly with T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes multiplicatively with T, e.g., thermal softening if c1<0)
- Thermal strain shift (thermoelasticity with thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress driven by mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Quadratic nonlinearity (geometric/material nonlinearity at moderate strain): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (nonlinear elastic response)
- Cubic polynomial elasticity (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (symmetric nonlinear elasticity around zero strain)
- Power-law strain hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic flow / hardening over a strain range)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = (c0 * epsilon**c1) * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening scaled by temperature-dependent softening/hardening)
- Offset strain / pre-strain model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (accounts for initial strain offset or fitting near yield)
- Saturating hardening (Voce-like rational form): sigma = c0 - c1 / (c2 * epsilon + c3) (approach to a saturation stress with increasing strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted form (implicit-style, written explicitly as a rational stress law): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon**c2) (captures transition from linear to nonlinear compliance)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable structure (no strain-rate term here): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (empirical plasticity with thermal softening via a temperature polynomial)
- Eyring/thermal-activation-inspired flow form: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (activated flow giving logarithmic-like stress growth with strain, modulated by T)
- Mixed coupling (nonseparable thermo-mechanical interaction): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 * T (captures coupling where temperature changes slope and curvature vs strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification → sigma approximately linear in epsilon with slope interpreted as an effective modulus; temperature dependence often appears as a multiplicative factor on epsilon.
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → multiplicative decreasing-in-T factors such as exp(c*T) with c<0, or low-order polynomials in T multiplying a strain term.
- Thermal expansion effects → stress depends on (epsilon - c*(T - T0)); i.e., a temperature-dependent horizontal shift of the stress–strain curve.
- Yield/transition behavior (elastic-to-plastic) → rational forms in epsilon or smooth nonlinear functions (e.g., asinh, tanh-like but not required) to create a knee without hard piecewise rules.
- Strain hardening → power laws epsilon**n or additive hardening terms (c0 + c1*epsilon**n); increasing concavity often indicates saturation-like hardening.
- Saturation stress at large strain → forms that asymptote to a constant (e.g., c0 - c1/(c2*epsilon+c3)) rather than unbounded growth.
- Nonseparable coupling (true thermo-mechanical interaction) → cross terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**m*T**n when temperature changes both slope and curvature with strain.
- Sign/odd symmetry considerations → odd powers of epsilon (epsilon, epsilon**3) model tension/compression symmetry near zero strain; even-power additions can break symmetry if data show it.

Key structural requirements:
- Exactly **three additive terms** with distinct structures:
  1) pure power in \(\epsilon\): \(\propto \epsilon^3\) (no \(T\)).
  2) \(\epsilon^{0.2143}\) times an **Arrhenius-in-\(1/T\)** factor: \(\exp(-K/T)\) (not \(\exp(KT)\)).
  3) \(\epsilon\) times a **quadratic polynomial in \(T\) with a shift**: \(\epsilon (T-327.264...)^2 = \epsilon(T^2 - 2\cdot 327.264\,T + 327.264^2)\). This necessarily contains both \(\epsilon T^2\) and \(\epsilon T\) components with linked coefficients.

Also, conditional equivalence allows \(\mathrm{Abs}(\epsilon)=\epsilon\) if we assume \(\epsilon\ge 0\).

1) \(T c0\epsilon + T c1\epsilon^2 + c2\epsilon + c3|\epsilon|^{c4} + c5 e^{T c6}|\epsilon|^{c7}\)  
Has \(\exp(T\cdot)\), not \(\exp(-K/T)\). Also lacks \(\epsilon(T-const)^2\) (needs \(T^2\epsilon\)). No.

6) Same: no Arrhenius, no \(\epsilon T^2\). No.

No.

12) \(Tc0\epsilon + Tc1\epsilon^2 + c2\epsilon + c3|\epsilon|^{c4} + c5\epsilon^3\).  
Can match the \(\epsilon^3\) term by setting \(c5=7.7229...\). But it still cannot produce the Arrhenius \(\epsilon^{0.2143}\exp(-K/T)\) term, and it cannot produce \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\) because it has only linear \(T\) dependence. No.

14) Has \(\exp(Tc4)\) not \(\exp(-K/T)\). No.

15) Saturating fraction \(|\epsilon|^{c6}/(c7+|\epsilon|^{c6})\); no Arrhenius; no \(\epsilon T^2\). No.

16) Has \(\exp(c4/T)\) which is of the right *type* (depends on \(1/T\)), but GT needs \(\exp(-K/T)\) multiplied by \(\epsilon^{0.2143}\) **and** also needs the \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\) term. Candidate 16’s exponential term is \(c3 \exp(c4/T)|\epsilon|^{c5}\) (good: can set \(c4<0\) and \(c5=0.2143\)), but the rest of candidate 16 is only \(T c0\epsilon + T c1\epsilon^2 + c2\epsilon\): still only linear in \(T\), so it cannot equal \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2\) which contains \(T^2\epsilon\). No.

17) Has \(\epsilon \exp(Tc6)\) wrong exponential and no \(\epsilon T^2\). No.

18)–37), 39), 49)–52)  
These are all complicated rational forms with denominators \((c1+|\epsilon|^{1/5})\) (or similar). GT is a **sum of simple monomials** in \(\epsilon\) plus one Arrhenius factor and one shifted quadratic in \(T\), with **no \(\epsilon\)-dependent denominators**. You could try to force the denominator to be constant by setting \(c1=0\), but then it becomes \(|\epsilon|^{1/5}\) in the denominator, still \(\epsilon\)-dependent; there is no parameter choice that removes the \(\epsilon\)-dependence of the denominator for all \(\epsilon\ge 0\). Therefore none of these can be identically equal to GT on a nontrivial domain. No for all of 18–37, 39, 49–52.

38) Has logs; GT has none. No.

No Arrhenius; no \(\epsilon T^2\). No.

No Arrhenius; no \(\epsilon T^2\). No.

48) \(Tc0\epsilon + Tc1\epsilon^2 + c2\epsilon + c3|\epsilon|^{c4} + c5\epsilon (T+c6)^{c7}\).  
This can represent the shifted-square term by setting \(c7=2\), \(c6=-327.264...\), \(c5=1.336133...\), and zeroing the linear-in-\(T\) nuisance terms (\(c0=c1=0\)). It can also represent the \(\epsilon^3\) term by setting \(c3=7.7229...\) and \(c4=3\) (assuming \(\epsilon\ge 0\) so \(|\epsilon|^3=\epsilon^3\)).

So none can match all three GT components simultaneously.

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon^3 + 36.659*epsilon^0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + 1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)^2`

Let me expand the last term:
`epsilon*(T - 327.264)^2 = epsilon*(T^2 - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`

So GT = `7.723*epsilon^3 + 36.659*epsilon^0.2144*exp(-9.916/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T^2 - 874.25*epsilon*T + 143,088*epsilon`

The GT has three fundamentally different basis function types:
1. **epsilon^3** (polynomial in epsilon)
2. **epsilon^0.2144 * exp(-c/T)** (fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential in T)
3. **epsilon*T^2, epsilon*T, epsilon** (polynomial cross-terms)

The key distinguishing feature is the **exp(-c/T)** term (Arrhenius). Let me check which candidates contain this or equivalent functionality.

**Candidates with exp(...):**
- **Candidate 1:** has `exp(T*c6)` — this is `exp(c*T)`, not `exp(c/T)`. NOT equivalent.
- **Candidate 5:** has `exp(T*c4)` — wait, no. Let me recheck. Candidate 5: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*Abs(epsilon)**c6` — no exp at all.
- **Candidate 14:** `c3*exp(T*c4)*Abs(epsilon)**c5` — `exp(c*T)` ≠ `exp(c/T)`.
- **Candidate 16:** `c3*exp(c4/T)*Abs(epsilon)**c5` — **This has exp(c/T)!**
- **Candidate 17:** `exp(T*c6)` — wrong form.

Let me check **Candidate 16** carefully:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon + c3*exp(c4/T)*Abs(epsilon)**c5`

GT needs: `a*epsilon*T^2 + b*epsilon*T + c*epsilon + d*epsilon^3 + e*epsilon^0.2144*exp(f/T)`

Candidate 16 has: `c0*T*epsilon + c1*T*epsilon^2 + c2*epsilon + c3*exp(c4/T)*epsilon^c5`

Missing: `epsilon*T^2` and `epsilon^3`. The candidate has `T*epsilon^2` but GT needs `epsilon*T^2` and `epsilon^3`. These are different basis functions. `T*epsilon^2 ≠ epsilon*T^2`. The candidate cannot produce the `epsilon*T^2` term. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 8:** `T^2*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon^2 + c3*epsilon + c4*Abs(epsilon)^c5`
This has `T^2*epsilon` (good!) and `T*epsilon` (good!) and `epsilon` (good!), but only one power `|epsilon|^c5`. GT needs both `epsilon^3` AND `epsilon^0.2144*exp(-c/T)`. No exp term. **NO MATCH.**

For all the rational-function candidates (18-52), they use combinations of polynomial and rational functions of epsilon with polynomial dependence on T. None can produce `exp(-c/T)`.

For candidates without exp(-c/T) or equivalent: The GT's Arrhenius term `exp(-c/T)` cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, or trigonometric functions. This rules out essentially all candidates.

Let me verify no candidate has `exp(c/T)`: Only **Candidate 16** has it, and it's missing the `T^2*epsilon` term.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can exactly match the GT.
